                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">عَزِيزٌ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form> 
                  <hi rend="ital">Mighty, potent, powerful,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">strong,</hi> [in an absolute sense; as also   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n28923-1" target="عَزٌّ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n28916"/></foreign>, accord. to the Msb; and especially,] <hi rend="ital">after lowness,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">meanness, of condition:</hi> (S, A, Msb:) [<hi rend="ital">high,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">elevated, in rank</hi> or <hi rend="ital">condition</hi> or <hi rend="ital">state; noble, honourable, glorious,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">illustrious:</hi> see <foreign lang="ar">عَزَّ</foreign>:] <hi rend="ital">rough in manners</hi> or <hi rend="ital">behaviour:</hi> (TA: [see <foreign lang="ar">ذَلِيلٌ</foreign>, which signifies, sometimes, the contr. of this:]) [<hi rend="ital">proud: disdainful; scornful; indignant:</hi> see <foreign lang="ar">عِزٌّ</foreign>:] <hi rend="ital">resisting; withstanding; indomitable; invincible; not to be overcome;</hi> applied to a man: (TA:) [<hi rend="ital">difficult,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">hard:</hi> and <hi rend="ital">impossible, insuperable,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">unattainable:</hi> see <foreign lang="ar">عَزَّ</foreign>:] <hi rend="ital">rare; scarce; hardly to be found:</hi> (S, K:) [and hence, <hi rend="ital">dear, highly esteemed,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">greatly valued:</hi> hence, also, applied to a word or phrase, <hi rend="ital">rare,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">extraordinary, in respect of usage</hi> or <hi rend="ital">analogy</hi> or <hi rend="ital">both:</hi>] and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n28923-2" target="أَعَزُّ" n="2" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n28929"/></foreign> also signifies the same as <foreign lang="ar">عَزِيزٌ</foreign> [mostly in the first of the senses expl. above, or in a similar sense]: (S, O, K:) and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n28923-3" target="عُزَّى" n="3" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n28927"/></foreign> the same as <foreign lang="ar">عَزِيزَةٌ</foreign> [app. as meaning <hi rend="ital">noble,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">the like</hi>], (O, K, TA,) applied to a woman: (TA:) the pl. of <foreign lang="ar">عَزِيزٌ</foreign> is <foreign lang="ar">عِزَازٌ</foreign> (S, O, K) and <foreign lang="ar">أَعِزَّةٌ</foreign> (S, Msb, K) and <foreign lang="ar">أَعِزَّآءُ</foreign>; (S, K;) but one does not say <foreign lang="ar">عُزَزَآءُ</foreign>, on account of the reduplication, which is disliked. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>    
      <foreign lang="ar">مَلِكٌ <ref cref="n28923-4" target="أَعَزُّ" n="4" type="1" subtype="SO" lang="ar" select="n28929"/></foreign> signifies the same as <foreign lang="ar">عَزِيزٌ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">A mighty, potent, powerful,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">strong, King;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">a glorious King</hi>]. (TA.) And El-Farezdak says, <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">إِنَّ ٱلَّذِى سَمَكَ السَّمَآءَ بَنَى لَنَا</foreign>
                     </L> 
                     <L><foreign lang="ar">بَيْتًا دَعَائِمُهُ <ref cref="n28923-5" target="أَعَرُّ" n="5" type="5" subtype="TFSO" lang="ar" select="n28525"/>وَأَطْوَلُ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> [<hi rend="ital">Verily He who raised the heaven built for us a tent of which the props are strong and tall</hi>]: meaning, <foreign lang="ar">عَزِيرَةٌ طَوِيلَةٌ</foreign>: like the phrase in the Kur [xxx. 26], <foreign lang="ar">وَهُوَ أَهْوَنُ عَلَيْهِ</foreign> [meaning <foreign lang="ar">هَيِّنٌ</foreign>]: not implying excess, accord. to ISd, because <foreign lang="ar">اَلْ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">مِنْ</foreign> supply each other's places [and one or the other of these, or a noun in the gen. case expressed or understood after the epithet, is necessary to denote excess: see <foreign lang="ar">أَكْبَرُ</foreign>]. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">العَزِيزُ</foreign>, as a name of God, signifies <hi rend="ital">The Mighty,</hi> (TA,) <hi rend="ital">who overcomes</hi> (O, TA) <hi rend="ital">everything:</hi> (TA:) or <hi rend="ital">He who resists,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">withstands, so that nothing overcomes Him:</hi> (Zj, TA:) or <hi rend="ital">The Incomparable,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">Unparalleled.</hi> (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  It also signifies <hi rend="ital">The King;</hi> because he has the mastery over the people of his dominions: (O, K:) and especially <hi rend="ital">the ruler of Misr together with Alexandria;</hi> (K, TA:) a surname; like <foreign lang="ar">النَّجَاشِىُّ</foreign> applied to the King of the Abyssinians, and <foreign lang="ar">قَيْصَرٌ</foreign> to the King of the Romans. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="5">-b5-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">وَإِنَّهُ لَكِتَابٌ عَزِيزٌ</foreign>, [said of the Kur, in that book, xli. 41, means <hi rend="ital">And verily it is a mighty book:</hi> meaning, <hi rend="ital">inimitable:</hi> or] <hi rend="ital">defended,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">protected,</hi> (Bd, Jel,) <hi rend="ital">from being rendered void and from being corrupted:</hi> (Bd:) or <hi rend="ital">of great utility; unequalled.</hi> (Bd.) [<foreign lang="ar">الكِتَابُ العَزِيزُ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">The mighty book,</hi> is an appellation often given to the Kur-án.]          <sense type="b" n="6">-b6-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">عِزُّ عَزِيزٌ</foreign> signifies <hi rend="ital">Great might,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">the like:</hi> or <hi rend="ital">might,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">the like, that is a cause of the same</hi> to a person. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="7">-b7-</sense>  It is said in the Kur [v. 59], <foreign lang="ar">فَسَوْفَ يَأْتِى ٱللّٰهُ بِقَوْمٍ يُحِبُّهُمْ وَيُحِبُّونَهُ أَذِلَّةٍ عَلَى</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">المُؤْمِنِينَ أَعِزَّةٍ عَلَى ٱلْكَافِرِينَ</foreign>, meaning, [<hi rend="ital">God will bring a people whom He will love and who will love Him,</hi>] <hi rend="ital">gentle to the believers, rough in manners,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">behaviour, to the unbelievers:</hi> (TA:) or <hi rend="ital">submissive to the believers,</hi> though they be [themselves] mighty, or noble, <hi rend="ital">proud to the unbelievers,</hi> though they be [themselves] inferior to them in highness of rank and in grounds of pretension to respect. (Az, TA.)          <sense type="b" n="8">-b8-</sense>  [And one says, <foreign lang="ar">هُوَ العَزِيزُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">أَنْ يُضَامَ</foreign>: expl. voce <foreign lang="ar">اَلْ</foreign> (p. 75). And <foreign lang="ar">هُوَ عَزِيزُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">النَّفْسِ</foreign>: see <foreign lang="ar">صُلْبٌ</foreign>. And <foreign lang="ar">اِمْرَأَةٌ عَزِيزَةٌ عَنْدَ نَفْسِهَا</foreign>: see <foreign lang="ar">ظَلِفٌ</foreign>.          <sense type="b" n="9">-b9-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">عَزِيزٌ</foreign> also signifies <hi rend="ital">Severe, difficult, distressing,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">grievous;</hi> (see an ex. voce <foreign lang="ar">عَنِتَ</foreign>;) and so   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n28923-6" target="أَعَزُّ" n="6" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n28929"/></foreign>, fem. <foreign lang="ar">عَزَّآءُ</foreign>:] you say, <foreign lang="ar">سَنَةٌ عَزَّآءُ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">A severe year:</hi> (S, O, K:) and <foreign lang="ar">مَنْ حَسُنَ مِنْهُ العَزَآءُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">هَآنَتْ عَلَيْهِ العَزَّآءُ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">He whose patient endurance of a loss is of a good description, what is difficult,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">distressing, becomes easy to him</hi>]. (A.)       <sense type="A" n="2">-A2-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">حَبُّ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">العَزِيزِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">The small tubercles that compose the root of the cyperus esculentus, which have a sweet and pleasant taste, and which women eat with the view of acquiring fatness thereby:</hi> and also <hi rend="ital">that plant itself:</hi> both are thus called in the present day]. (TA voce <foreign lang="ar">سُقَّيْطٌ</foreign>, &amp;c.)    </entryFree>2d:T1445,<entryFree id="n28929" key="أَعَزُّ" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">أَعَزُّ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form> [<hi rend="ital">More,</hi> and <hi rend="ital">most, mighty, potent, powerful,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">strong:</hi> &amp;c.: see <foreign lang="ar">عَزِيزٌ</foreign>, of which it is the comparative and superlative form: and see an ex. voce <foreign lang="ar">اَلْ</foreign> (p. 75): and another in a verse cited in art. <foreign lang="ar">صب</foreign>, conj. 6]. It is related in a trad. of Aboo-Bekr, that he said to 'Áïsheh, <foreign lang="ar">إِنَّ أَحَبَّ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">النَّاسِ إِلَىَّ غَنًى أَنْتِ وَأَعَزُّهُمْ فَقْرًا أَنْتِ</foreign>, meaning. <hi rend="ital">Verily the one of mankind whose richness is most pleasing to me art thou; and the one of them whose poverty is most distressing to me art thou.</hi> (Mgh.) The fem. of <foreign lang="ar">أَعَزُّ</foreign> [as a noun of excess] is   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n28929-1" target="عُزَّى" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n28927"/></foreign>: (S, ISd, O, K;) like as <foreign lang="ar">فُضْلَى</foreign> is of <foreign lang="ar">أَفْضَلُ</foreign>. (ISd.) [But see what follows.]          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>    
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n28929-2" target="العُزَّى" n="2" type="1" subtype="SO" lang="ar"/></foreign> was the name of <hi rend="ital">A certain idol,</hi> (S, O, K,) <hi rend="ital">belonging to Kureysh and Benoo-Kináneh:</hi> (S, O, TA:) or <hi rend="ital">a certain gum-acacia-tree,</hi> (<foreign lang="ar">سَمُرَةٌ</foreign>,) <hi rend="ital">which the tribe of Ghatafán</hi> (S, O, K) <hi rend="ital">the son of Saad the son of Keys-'Eilán</hi> (TA) <hi rend="ital">used to worship;</hi> (S, O, K;) <hi rend="ital">the first who took it as an object of worship was Dhálim the son of As' ad; above Dhát- 'Irk, nine miles towards El-Bustán,</hi> (O, K, TA,) <hi rend="ital">at</hi> [<hi rend="ital">the valley called</hi>] <hi rend="ital">En-Nakhleh Esh-Shámeeyeh,</hi> (O, TA,) <hi rend="ital">near Mekkeh; or, as some say, at Et- Táïf:</hi> (TA:) he, (K,) Dhálim, (O,) or they, (S,) built over it a house, (S, O, K) and named it <foreign lang="ar">بُسّ</foreign>, (O, K,) accord. to Ibn-El-Kelbee; or, accord. to others, <foreign lang="ar">بُسَّآء</foreign>; (TA;) and they appointed to it ministers, (S, TA,) like those of the Kaabeh; (TA;) and they used to hear in it a voice: (O, K, TA:) but Mohammad sent to it Khálid Ibn-El-Weleed, (S, O, K,) in the year of the conquest [of Mekkeh], (O, TA,) and he demolished the house, (S, K,) and slew the [chief] minister, (TA,) and burned the gum-acacia-tree: (S, O, K:) or, as is related on the authority of I'Ab, <hi rend="ital">a certain she-devil,</hi> who used to come to three gumacacia-trees (<foreign lang="ar">سَمُرَات</foreign>) in Batn-Nakhleh, against whom Mohammad, when he conquered Mekkeh, <pb n="2033"/> sent Khálid Ibn-El-Weleed; and he cut down the trees, and slew her and her minister. (TA.) A poet says, <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">أَمَا وَدِمَآءٍ مَائِرَاتٍ تَخَالُهَا</foreign>
                     </L> 
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">عَلَى قُنَّةِ العُزَّى وَبِالنَّسْرِ عَنْدَمَا</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> [<hi rend="ital">Verily,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">now surely, by bloods flowing, and running hither and thither, which thou wouldst think to be dragon's-blood, upon the mountain-top of El-' Ozzà, and by En-Nesr</hi>]. (S.) ISd says, I hold   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n28929-3" target="العُزَّى" n="3" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> to be fem. of <foreign lang="ar">الأَعَزُّ</foreign>; and if so, the <foreign lang="ar">ال</foreign> in the former is not redundant, but is like the <foreign lang="ar">ال</foreign> in <foreign lang="ar">الحَارِثُ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">العَبَّاسُ</foreign>: but properly it should be redundant, because we have not heard <foreign lang="ar">العُزَّى</foreign> as an epithet [of excess] like as we have heard <foreign lang="ar">الصُّغْرَى</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">الكُبْرَى</foreign>. (L, TA.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>    
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n28929-4" target="عُزَّى" n="4" type="1" subtype="SO" lang="ar" select="n28927"/></foreign> is [however] used in the sense of <foreign lang="ar">عَزِيزَةٌ</foreign>: (K, TA:) and <foreign lang="ar">أَعَزُّ</foreign> [fem. <foreign lang="ar">عَزَّآءُ</foreign>] is also syn. with <foreign lang="ar">عَزِيزٌ</foreign>, which see in four places.
